4905</div>

4906

4907 </section>

4908

4909

4910

4911 <section id="_90">

4912

4913 <h2>

4914Treatment of Recurrent Childhood High-Grade Astrocytomas</h2>

4915

4916 <div id="_section_90" class="pdq-sections">

4917<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4918<h6>

4919In This Section</h6>

4920<ul>

4921<li>

4922<a href="#_1874_toc">

4923Surgery</a>

4924</li>

4925<li>

4926<a href="#_1875_toc">

4927High-dose Chemotherapy With SCT</a>

4928</li>

4929<li>

4930<a href="#_1876_toc">

4931Radiation Therapy</a>

4932</li>

4933<li>

4934<a href="#_1879_toc">

4935Targeted Therapy</a>

4936</li>

4937<li>

4938<a href="#_1924_toc">

4939Immunotherapy</a>

4940</li>

4941<li>

4942<a href="#_136_toc">

4943Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation<ul>

4944<li>

4945<a href="#_TrialSearch_136_sid_13_toc">

4946Current Clinical Trials</a>

4947</li>

4948</ul>

4949</a>

4950</li>

4951</ul>

4952</nav>

4953<p id="_1870" tabindex="-1">

4954To determine and implement optimal management, treatment of childhood high-grade astrocytomas should be guided by a multidisciplinary team of cancer specialists who have experience treating childhood brain tumors. </p>

4955<p id="_91" tabindex="-1">

4956Most patients with high-grade astrocytomas or gliomas will eventually have tumor recurrence. Recurrences usually occur within 3 years of original diagnosis, but some patients recur many years after initial treatment. Disease may recur at the primary tumor site, at the margin of the resection/radiation bed, or at noncontiguous central nervous system sites. Systemic relapse rarely occurs. </p>

4957<p id="_334" tabindex="-1">

4958At the time of recurrence, a complete evaluation for extent of relapse is indicated for all malignant tumors. Biopsy or surgical resection may be necessary for confirmation of relapse because other entities, such as secondary tumor and treatment-related brain necrosis, may be clinically indistinguishable from tumor recurrence. </p>

4959<p id="_452" tabindex="-1">

4960Treatment options for recurrent childhood high-grade astrocytomas include the following:</p>

4961<div class="pdq-content-list">

4962<ol id="_453">

4963<li>

4964<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1874">

4965Surgery</a>

4966.</li>

4967<li>

4968<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1875">

4969High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell transplant (SCT)</a>

4970.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

49711</a>

4972]</li>

4973<li>

4974<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1876">

4975Radiation therapy</a>

4976.</li>

4977<li>

4978<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1879">

4979Targeted therapy</a>

4980 with a BRAF inhibitor, for patients with a <em class="gene-name">

4981BRAF</em>

4982 V600E mutation.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

49832</a>

4984]</li>

4985<li>

4986<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1924">

4987Immunotherapy</a>

4988.</li>

4989</ol>

4990</div>

4991<section id="_1874">

4992<h3 id="_1874_toc">

4993Surgery</h3>

4994<p id="_454" tabindex="-1">

4995The utility of surgical intervention must be individualized on the basis of the following: </p>

4996<div class="pdq-content-list">

4997<ul id="_335">

4998<li>

4999Initial tumor type.</li>

5000<li>

5001Length of time between initial treatment and the reappearance of the mass lesion.</li>

5002<li>

5003Location of the recurrent tumor.</li>

5004<li>

5005Consideration of therapeutics based on the requirement for fresh tumor tissue or to deliver therapy to the operative bed.</li>

5006</ul>

5007</div>

5008</section>

5009<section id="_1875">

5010<h3 id="_1875_toc">

5011High-dose Chemotherapy With SCT</h3>

5012<p id="_92" tabindex="-1">

5013High-dose, marrow-ablative chemotherapy with hematopoietic SCT may be effective in a highly selected subset of patients with minimal residual disease at time of recurrence.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

50141</a>

5015][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5016Level of evidence C1</a>

5017] However, the results of previous clinical trials that tested various targeted and combination chemotherapies have largely failed to demonstrate convincing benefits for enrolled patients.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

50183</a>

5019-<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

50205</a>

5021]</p>

5022</section>

5023<section id="_1876">

5024<h3 id="_1876_toc">

5025Radiation Therapy</h3>

5026<p id="_1877" tabindex="-1">

5027Radiation therapy is appropriate for patients who have not previously been irradiated. Radiation doses and volumes are similar to those used for newly diagnosed patients. Generally, this is limited to young children initially treated with radiation-avoiding strategies. </p>

5028<p id="_1878" tabindex="-1">

5029For previously irradiated patients, reirradiation has been used, although the data demonstrating benefit are sparse. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46701&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=NotSet" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046701&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=NotSet'); return(false);">

5030Stereotactic radiosurgery (SRS)</a>

5031 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44464&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=NotSet" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044464&amp;version=healthprofessional&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=NotSet'); return(false);">

5032stereotactic radiation therapy (SRT)</a>

5033 techniques using either hypofractionated radiation therapy or standard fraction sizes may be considered. For small volume distinct lesions, SRS allows for maximum sparing of normal tissues. For more infiltrative lesions, fractionated radiation therapy may better spare normal tissues.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

50346</a>

5035]</p>

5036</section>

5037<section id="_1879">

5038<h3 id="_1879_toc">

5039Targeted Therapy</h3>

5040<p id="_433" tabindex="-1">

5041Molecular targets for recurrent high-grade gliomas are limited. <em class="gene-name">

5042BRAF</em>

5043 V600E mutations are present in a small subset of these patients, and a small number of cases have responded to BRAF inhibitors.</p>

5044<p id="_1891" tabindex="-1">

5045A case report documented a complete response to the BRAF inhibitor vemurafenib in a patient with recurrent <em class="gene-name">

5046BRAF</em>

5047 V600&#8211;mutated glioblastoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

50487</a>

5049] A phase I study reported in an abstract that eight children with progressive <em class="gene-name">

5050BRAF</em>

5051 V600E high-grade gliomas were treated with dabrafenib and demonstrated three complete responses, three partial responses, and two progressive disease responses.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

50528</a>

5053]</p>

5054<p id="_1901" tabindex="-1">

5055A small percentage of children with high-grade gliomas have gene fusions involving tyrosine kinases (e.g., <em class="gene-name">

5056ALK</em>

5057, <em class="gene-name">

5058NTRK1</em>

5059, <em class="gene-name">

5060NTRK2</em>

5061, <em class="gene-name">

5062NTRK3</em>

5063, <em class="gene-name">

5064ROS1</em>

5065, and <em class="gene-name">

5066MET</em>

5067).[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

50689</a>

5069,<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

507010</a>

5071] Kinase gene fusions account for a high percentage of cases among children younger than 1 year, but they can occur throughout childhood. Case reports have described responses to kinase inhibitors for patients with relapsed or refractory high-grade gliomas who have these gene fusions.[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

507211</a>

5073,<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

507412</a>

5075]</p>

5076</section>

5077<section id="_1924">

5078<h3 id="_1924_toc">

5079Immunotherapy</h3>

5080<p id="_1925" tabindex="-1">

5081Numerous studies are investigating a variety of immunotherapy strategies, including checkpoint inhibitors, oncolytic viruses, and other immune-modulating strategies. The utility of such strategies in the treatment of patients with recurrent childhood high-grade astrocytomas is unproven, with only preliminary evidence of activity in some settings.[<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

508213</a>

5083]</p>

5084</section>

5085<section id="_136">

5086<h3 id="_136_toc">

5087Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation</h3>

5088<p id="_488" tabindex="-1">

5089The role of immune checkpoint inhibition in the treatment of children with recurrent high-grade astrocytoma is currently under study. Children with biallelic mismatch repair deficiency have a very high mutational burden and neoantigen expression and are at risk of developing a variety of cancers, including hematologic malignancies, gastrointestinal cancers, and brain tumors. The high mutation and neoantigen load has been correlated with improved response to immune checkpoint inhibition. Early case reports have demonstrated clinical and radiographic responses in children who are treated with an anti&#8211;programmed death-1 (anti&#8211;PD-1) inhibitor.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

509014</a>

5091]</p>

5092<p id="_1796" tabindex="-1">

5093Patients for whom initial treatment fails may benefit from additional treatment, including entry into clinical trials of novel therapeutic approaches.[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

509415</a>

5095] Early-phase therapeutic trials may be available for selected patients. These trials may be available via the <a href="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/" title="https://www.childrensoncologygroup.org/">

5096Children's Oncology Group (COG)</a>

5097, the <a href="http://www.pbtc.org/" title="http://www.pbtc.org/">

5098Pediatric Brain Tumor Consortium</a>

5099, or other entities. Information about NCI-supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

5100NCI website</a>

5101. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, refer to the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

5102ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

5103.</p>

5104<p id="_1800" tabindex="-1">

5105The following is an example of a national and/or institutional clinical trial that is currently being conducted:</p>

5106<div class="pdq-content-list">

5107<ul id="_1797">

5108<li>

5109<strong>

5110<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03155620">

5111APEC1621 (NCT03155620)</a>

5112</strong>

5113 (Pediatric MATCH: Targeted Therapy Directed by Genetic Testing in Treating Pediatric Patients with Relapsed or Refractory Advanced Solid Tumors, Non-Hodgkin Lymphomas, or Histiocytic Disorders)<strong>

5114:</strong>

5115 NCI-COG Pediatric Molecular Analysis for Therapeutic Choice (MATCH), referred to as Pediatric MATCH, will match targeted agents with specific molecular changes identified in a patient's tumor (refractory or recurrent). Children and adolescents aged 1 to 21 years are eligible for the trial.<p id="_1808" tabindex="-1">

5116Patients with tumors that have molecular variants addressed by treatment arms included in the trial will be offered treatment on Pediatric MATCH. Additional information can be obtained on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match">

5117NCI website</a>

5118 and <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620">

5119ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

5120.</p>

5121

5122</li>

5123</ul>

5124</div>

5125<section id="_TrialSearch_136_sid_13">

5126<h4 id="_TrialSearch_136_sid_13_toc">

5127Current Clinical Trials</h4>

5128<p id="_TrialSearch_136_22" tabindex="-1">

5129Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5130advanced clinical trial search</a>

5131 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5132General information</a>

5133 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

5190Bouffet E, Larouche V, Campbell BB, et al.: Immune Checkpoint Inhibition for Hypermutant Glioblastoma Multiforme Resulting From Germline Biallelic Mismatch Repair Deficiency. J Clin Oncol 34 (19): 2206-11, 2016.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=27001570&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=27001570&amp;dopt=Abstract">

5191[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

5192</li>

5193<li id="section_7.15">

5194Warren KE, Gururangan S, Geyer JR, et al.: A phase II study of O6-benzylguanine and temozolomide in pediatric patients with recurrent or progressive high-grade gliomas and brainstem gliomas: a Pediatric Brain Tumor Consortium study. J Neurooncol 106 (3): 643-9, 2012.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=21968943&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=21968943&amp;dopt=Abstract">

5195[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

5196</li>

5197</ol>

5198</div>

5199

5200 </section>

5201

5202

5203

5204 <section id="_78">

5205

5206 <h2>

5207Changes to This Summary (04/19/2022)</h2>

5208

5209 <div id="_section_78" class="pdq-sections">

5210<p id="_153" tabindex="-1">

5211The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as new information becomes available. This section describes the latest changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

5212<p id="_1946" tabindex="-1">

5213<strong>

5214<a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_306">

5215Treatment of Childhood Low-Grade Astrocytomas</a>

5216</strong>

5217</p>

5218<p id="_1947" tabindex="-1">

5219Added <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_307">

5220text</a>

5221 to state that surgical resection for spinal tumors is generally attempted but it often cannot be completed. Also added text about the results of a study that included 128 patients with primary spinal cord low-grade gliomas, including information about treatment, outcomes, and complications (cited Perwein et al. as reference 13 and level of evidence 3iiiDi).</p>

5222<p id="_1948" tabindex="-1">

5223Added <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_1945">

5224text</a>

5225 to state that a multivariate analysis examined 100 patients with confirmed diagnoses of World Health Organization (WHO) grade II diffuse gliomas treated in an International Society of Paediatric Oncology study. The extent of glioma resection had the greatest impact on patients' event-free survival (EFS) rates. The 5-year EFS rates were 75% to 76% for patients who underwent a complete or subtotal resection. In comparison, 5-year EFS rates were 56% for patients who had a partial resection and 19% for patients who had a biopsy (cited Falkenstein et al. as reference 17 and level of evidence 2Di).</p>

5226<p id="_1949" tabindex="-1">

5227Added <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_412">

5228text</a>

5229 to state that in a separate study that included 100 patients with WHO grade II diffuse gliomas, a subset of patients were treated with carboplatin and vincristine; some patients also received etoposide. This subset of patients had a 5-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate of 38% when patients with <em class="gene-name">

5230Histone3</em>

5231-mutated tumors were excluded.</p>

5232<p id="_1950" tabindex="-1">

5233Added <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_483">

5234text</a>

5235 to state that in a separate study that included 100 patients with WHO grade II diffuse gliomas, a subset of patients were treated with radiation therapy. These patients had a 5-year PFS rate of 74% when patients with <em class="gene-name">

5236Histone3</em>

5237-mutated tumors were excluded.</p>

5238<p id="_disclaimerHP_3" tabindex="-1">

5239This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

5240PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5241, which is

5242editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

5243the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

5244information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

5245maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

5246About This PDQ Summary</a>

5247 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

5248PDQ&#174; Cancer Information for Health Professionals</a>

5249 pages.

5250</p>

5251</div>

5252

5253 </section>

5257 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

5258

5259 <h2>

5260About This PDQ Summary</h2>

5261

5262 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

5263<section id="_AboutThis_2">

5264<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

5265Purpose of This Summary</h3>

5266<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

5267This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of childhood astrocytomas. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

5268</section>

5269<section id="_AboutThis_4">

5270<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

5271Reviewers and Updates</h3>

5272<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

5273This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

5274PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5275, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

5276<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

5277 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

5278<div class="pdq-content-list">

5279<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

5280<li>

5281be discussed at a meeting,</li>

5282<li>

5283be cited with text, or</li>

5284<li>

5285replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

5286</ul>

5287</div>

5288<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

5289Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

5290<p id="" tabindex="-1">

5291The lead reviewers for Childhood Astrocytomas Treatment are:</p>

5292<div class="pdq-content-list">

5293<ul id="">

5294<li>

5295Kenneth J. Cohen, MD, MBA (Sidney Kimmel Comprehensive Cancer Center at Johns Hopkins Hospital)</li>

5296<li>

5297Louis S. Constine, MD (James P. Wilmot Cancer Center at University of Rochester Medical Center)</li>

5298<li>

5299Karen J. Marcus, MD, FACR (Dana-Farber Cancer Institute/Boston Children's Hospital)</li>

5300<li>

5301Roger J. Packer, MD (Children's National Hospital)</li>

5302<li>

5303D. Williams Parsons, MD, PhD (Texas Children's Hospital)</li>

5304<li>

5305Malcolm A. Smith, MD, PhD (National Cancer Institute)</li>

5306</ul>

5307</div>

5308<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5309Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5310Email Us</a>

5311. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5312</section>

5313<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5314<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5315Levels of Evidence</h3>

5316<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5317Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5318formal evidence ranking system</a>

5319 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5320</section>

5321<section id="_AboutThis_12">

5322<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

5323Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

5324<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

5325PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

5326<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

5327The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

5328<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

5329PDQ&#174; Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Childhood Astrocytomas Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq">

5330https://www.cancer.gov/types/brain/hp/child-astrocytoma-treament-pdq</a>

5331. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389382]</p>

5333Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">
